        "before": "Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md\n=== architecture.md ===\n# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation\n\n---\n\n## Section 1: Backend System Design\n\n### 1. Flask Application Structure\n\nThe Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:\n\n- `app.py` (entry point)\n- `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)\n- `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)\n- `services/` (business logic and version control management)\n- `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)\n- `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)\n\n#### Module Responsibilities:\n\n- **app.py**\n  - Initialize Flask app instance.\n  - Register blueprints from `routes/`.\n  - Setup session configuration and error handlers.\n\n- **routes/**\n  - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.\n  - Handle request input (GET/POST data).\n  - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.\n  - Render templates with provided context variables.\n\n- **models/**\n  - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).\n  - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.\n  - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.\n  - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.\n\n- **services/**\n  - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.\n  - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).\n  - Handle validation logic for input data.\n  - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.\n\n- **utils/**\n  - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.\n  - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.\n  - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.\n\n- **data/**\n  - Storage location for all app data text files.\n  - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.\n\n### Data Flow Between Components\n\n1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.\n2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).\n3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.\n4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.\n5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.\n6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.\n\nThis layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.\n\n---\n\n## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints\n\nBelow is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.\n\n| Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |\n|---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user\nOutput: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |\n| `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.\nPOST: Form data for new article draft.\nOutput: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.\nPOST: updated article data for new version.\nOutput: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.\nOutput: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |\n| `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.\nOutput: list of user's articles and filter status. |\n| `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.\nOutput: list of published articles. |\n| `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.\nPOST: receives scheduling data.\nOutput: updated schedule or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.\nOutput: renders analytics data structured for display. |\n\n### Route Input & Output Details\n\n- Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.\n- Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.\n- User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.\n- Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Version Control Design\n\n### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow\n\n- **Article Versions:**\n  - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:\n    - `version_id` (unique),\n    - `article_id` link,\n    - `version_number` (incremented per article),\n    - `content` (full textual content),\n    - `author` username,\n    - `created_date` timestamp,\n    - `change_summary` (one-line description).\n  - New versions created on edits.\n\n- **Approval Workflow:**\n  - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.\n  - Each approval entry:\n    - `approval_id` unique,\n    - `article_id`,\n    - `version_id`,\n    - `approver` username,\n    - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),\n    - `comments` text,\n    - `timestamp`.\n  - Multiple approvers may act on same version.\n\n- **Comments:**\n  - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.\n\n- **Workflow Stages:**\n  - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.\n  - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.\n\n### Interaction with Storage\n\n- On article edit:\n  - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.\n  - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.\n\n- On approval action:\n  - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.\n\n- Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.\n\n- Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.\n\n---\n\n## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points\n\n- Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.\n- Context variables include:\n  - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.\n  - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.\n  - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.\n\n- JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.\n\n- Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.\n\n- Coordination Points with Frontend Team:\n  - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).\n  - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.\n  - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.\n  - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.\n\n- Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.\n\n- Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.\n\n---\n\nThis architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.\n\nAll implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.\n\n",

        "before": "Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md\n=== architecture.md ===\n# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation\n\n---\n\n## Section 1: Backend System Design\n\n### 1. Flask Application Structure\n\nThe Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:\n\n- `app.py` (entry point)\n- `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)\n- `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)\n- `services/` (business logic and version control management)\n- `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)\n- `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)\n\n#### Module Responsibilities:\n\n- **app.py**\n  - Initialize Flask app instance.\n  - Register blueprints from `routes/`.\n  - Setup session configuration and error handlers.\n\n- **routes/**\n  - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.\n  - Handle request input (GET/POST data).\n  - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.\n  - Render templates with provided context variables.\n\n- **models/**\n  - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).\n  - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.\n  - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.\n  - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.\n\n- **services/**\n  - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.\n  - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).\n  - Handle validation logic for input data.\n  - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.\n\n- **utils/**\n  - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.\n  - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.\n  - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.\n\n- **data/**\n  - Storage location for all app data text files.\n  - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.\n\n### Data Flow Between Components\n\n1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.\n2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).\n3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.\n4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.\n5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.\n6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.\n\nThis layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.\n\n---\n\n## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints\n\nBelow is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.\n\n| Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |\n|---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user\nOutput: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |\n| `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.\nPOST: Form data for new article draft.\nOutput: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.\nPOST: updated article data for new version.\nOutput: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.\nOutput: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |\n| `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.\nOutput: list of user's articles and filter status. |\n| `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.\nOutput: list of published articles. |\n| `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.\nPOST: receives scheduling data.\nOutput: updated schedule or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.\nOutput: renders analytics data structured for display. |\n\n### Route Input & Output Details\n\n- Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.\n- Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.\n- User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.\n- Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Version Control Design\n\n### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow\n\n- **Article Versions:**\n  - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:\n    - `version_id` (unique),\n    - `article_id` link,\n    - `version_number` (incremented per article),\n    - `content` (full textual content),\n    - `author` username,\n    - `created_date` timestamp,\n    - `change_summary` (one-line description).\n  - New versions created on edits.\n\n- **Approval Workflow:**\n  - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.\n  - Each approval entry:\n    - `approval_id` unique,\n    - `article_id`,\n    - `version_id`,\n    - `approver` username,\n    - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),\n    - `comments` text,\n    - `timestamp`.\n  - Multiple approvers may act on same version.\n\n- **Comments:**\n  - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.\n\n- **Workflow Stages:**\n  - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.\n  - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.\n\n### Interaction with Storage\n\n- On article edit:\n  - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.\n  - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.\n\n- On approval action:\n  - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.\n\n- Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.\n\n- Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.\n\n---\n\n## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points\n\n- Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.\n- Context variables include:\n  - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.\n  - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.\n  - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.\n\n- JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.\n\n- Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.\n\n- Coordination Points with Frontend Team:\n  - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).\n  - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.\n  - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.\n  - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.\n\n- Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.\n\n- Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.\n\n---\n\nThis architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.\n\nAll implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.\n\n",

        "before": "Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md\n=== architecture.md ===\n# ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation\n\n---\n\n## Section 1: Backend System Design\n\n### 1. Flask Application Structure\n\nThe Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:\n\n- `app.py` (entry point)\n- `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)\n- `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)\n- `services/` (business logic and version control management)\n- `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)\n- `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)\n\n#### Module Responsibilities:\n\n- **app.py**\n  - Initialize Flask app instance.\n  - Register blueprints from `routes/`.\n  - Setup session configuration and error handlers.\n\n- **routes/**\n  - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.\n  - Handle request input (GET/POST data).\n  - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.\n  - Render templates with provided context variables.\n\n- **models/**\n  - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).\n  - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.\n  - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.\n  - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.\n\n- **services/**\n  - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.\n  - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).\n  - Handle validation logic for input data.\n  - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.\n\n- **utils/**\n  - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.\n  - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.\n  - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.\n\n- **data/**\n  - Storage location for all app data text files.\n  - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.\n\n### Data Flow Between Components\n\n1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.\n2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).\n3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.\n4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.\n5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.\n6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.\n\nThis layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.\n\n---\n\n## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints\n\nBelow is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.\n\n| Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |\n|---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|\n| `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user\nOutput: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |\n| `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.\nPOST: Form data for new article draft.\nOutput: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.\nPOST: updated article data for new version.\nOutput: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.\nOutput: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |\n| `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.\nOutput: list of user's articles and filter status. |\n| `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.\nOutput: list of published articles. |\n| `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.\nPOST: receives scheduling data.\nOutput: updated schedule or errors. |\n| `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.\nOutput: renders analytics data structured for display. |\n\n### Route Input & Output Details\n\n- Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.\n- Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.\n- User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.\n- Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.\n\n---\n\n## Section 3: Version Control Design\n\n### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow\n\n- **Article Versions:**\n  - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:\n    - `version_id` (unique),\n    - `article_id` link,\n    - `version_number` (incremented per article),\n    - `content` (full textual content),\n    - `author` username,\n    - `created_date` timestamp,\n    - `change_summary` (one-line description).\n  - New versions created on edits.\n\n- **Approval Workflow:**\n  - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.\n  - Each approval entry:\n    - `approval_id` unique,\n    - `article_id`,\n    - `version_id`,\n    - `approver` username,\n    - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),\n    - `comments` text,\n    - `timestamp`.\n  - Multiple approvers may act on same version.\n\n- **Comments:**\n  - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.\n\n- **Workflow Stages:**\n  - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.\n  - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.\n\n### Interaction with Storage\n\n- On article edit:\n  - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.\n  - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.\n\n- On approval action:\n  - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.\n\n- Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.\n\n- Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.\n\n---\n\n## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points\n\n- Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.\n- Context variables include:\n  - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.\n  - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.\n  - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.\n\n- JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.\n\n- Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.\n\n- Coordination Points with Frontend Team:\n  - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).\n  - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.\n  - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.\n  - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.\n\n- Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.\n\n- Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.\n\n---\n\nThis architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.\n\nAll implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.\n\n",

      📄 Before (full content):
         Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md
         === architecture.md ===
         # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 1: Backend System Design
         
         ### 1. Flask Application Structure
         
         The Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:
         
         - `app.py` (entry point)
         - `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)
         - `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)
         - `services/` (business logic and version control management)
         - `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)
         - `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)
         
         #### Module Responsibilities:
         
         - **app.py**
           - Initialize Flask app instance.
           - Register blueprints from `routes/`.
           - Setup session configuration and error handlers.
         
         - **routes/**
           - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.
           - Handle request input (GET/POST data).
           - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.
           - Render templates with provided context variables.
         
         - **models/**
           - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).
           - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.
           - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.
           - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.
         
         - **services/**
           - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.
           - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).
           - Handle validation logic for input data.
           - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.
         
         - **utils/**
           - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.
           - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.
           - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.
         
         - **data/**
           - Storage location for all app data text files.
           - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.
         
         ### Data Flow Between Components
         
         1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.
         2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).
         3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.
         4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.
         5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.
         6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.
         
         This layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints
         
         Below is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.
         
         | Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |
         |---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|
         | `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user
         Output: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |
         | `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.
         POST: Form data for new article draft.
         Output: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.
         POST: updated article data for new version.
         Output: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.
         Output: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |
         | `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.
         Output: list of user's articles and filter status. |
         | `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.
         Output: list of published articles. |
         | `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.
         POST: receives scheduling data.
         Output: updated schedule or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.
         Output: renders analytics data structured for display. |
         
         ### Route Input & Output Details
         
         - Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.
         - Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.
         - User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.
         - Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 3: Version Control Design
         
         ### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow
         
         - **Article Versions:**
           - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:
             - `version_id` (unique),
             - `article_id` link,
             - `version_number` (incremented per article),
             - `content` (full textual content),
             - `author` username,
             - `created_date` timestamp,
             - `change_summary` (one-line description).
           - New versions created on edits.
         
         - **Approval Workflow:**
           - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.
           - Each approval entry:
             - `approval_id` unique,
             - `article_id`,
             - `version_id`,
             - `approver` username,
             - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),
             - `comments` text,
             - `timestamp`.
           - Multiple approvers may act on same version.
         
         - **Comments:**
           - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.
         
         - **Workflow Stages:**
           - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.
           - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.
         
         ### Interaction with Storage
         
         - On article edit:
           - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.
           - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.
         
         - On approval action:
           - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.
         
         - Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.
         
         - Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points
         
         - Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.
         - Context variables include:
           - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.
           - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.
           - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.
         
         - JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.
         
         - Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.
         
         - Coordination Points with Frontend Team:
           - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).
           - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.
           - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.
           - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.
         
         - Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.
         
         - Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.
         
         ---
         
         This architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.
         
         All implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.

      📄 Before (full content):
         Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md
         === architecture.md ===
         # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 1: Backend System Design
         
         ### 1. Flask Application Structure
         
         The Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:
         
         - `app.py` (entry point)
         - `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)
         - `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)
         - `services/` (business logic and version control management)
         - `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)
         - `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)
         
         #### Module Responsibilities:
         
         - **app.py**
           - Initialize Flask app instance.
           - Register blueprints from `routes/`.
           - Setup session configuration and error handlers.
         
         - **routes/**
           - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.
           - Handle request input (GET/POST data).
           - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.
           - Render templates with provided context variables.
         
         - **models/**
           - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).
           - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.
           - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.
           - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.
         
         - **services/**
           - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.
           - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).
           - Handle validation logic for input data.
           - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.
         
         - **utils/**
           - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.
           - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.
           - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.
         
         - **data/**
           - Storage location for all app data text files.
           - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.
         
         ### Data Flow Between Components
         
         1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.
         2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).
         3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.
         4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.
         5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.
         6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.
         
         This layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints
         
         Below is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.
         
         | Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |
         |---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|
         | `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user
         Output: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |
         | `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.
         POST: Form data for new article draft.
         Output: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.
         POST: updated article data for new version.
         Output: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.
         Output: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |
         | `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.
         Output: list of user's articles and filter status. |
         | `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.
         Output: list of published articles. |
         | `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.
         POST: receives scheduling data.
         Output: updated schedule or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.
         Output: renders analytics data structured for display. |
         
         ### Route Input & Output Details
         
         - Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.
         - Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.
         - User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.
         - Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 3: Version Control Design
         
         ### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow
         
         - **Article Versions:**
           - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:
             - `version_id` (unique),
             - `article_id` link,
             - `version_number` (incremented per article),
             - `content` (full textual content),
             - `author` username,
             - `created_date` timestamp,
             - `change_summary` (one-line description).
           - New versions created on edits.
         
         - **Approval Workflow:**
           - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.
           - Each approval entry:
             - `approval_id` unique,
             - `article_id`,
             - `version_id`,
             - `approver` username,
             - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),
             - `comments` text,
             - `timestamp`.
           - Multiple approvers may act on same version.
         
         - **Comments:**
           - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.
         
         - **Workflow Stages:**
           - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.
           - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.
         
         ### Interaction with Storage
         
         - On article edit:
           - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.
           - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.
         
         - On approval action:
           - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.
         
         - Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.
         
         - Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points
         
         - Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.
         - Context variables include:
           - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.
           - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.
           - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.
         
         - JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.
         
         - Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.
         
         - Coordination Points with Frontend Team:
           - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).
           - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.
           - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.
           - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.
         
         - Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.
         
         - Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.
         
         ---
         
         This architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.
         
         All implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.

         Implement Flask backend app.py with routing, data models, version control, approvals, comments, and analytics per architecture.md
         === architecture.md ===
         # ContentPublishingHub Backend Architecture Documentation
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 1: Backend System Design
         
         ### 1. Flask Application Structure
         
         The Flask application for ContentPublishingHub is structured into the following main modules and packages:
         
         - `app.py` (entry point)
         - `routes/` (package containing route controllers for different URL endpoints)
         - `models/` (package for data access and manipulation layer)
         - `services/` (business logic and version control management)
         - `utils/` (utility functions such as file I/O, validation, session management)
         - `data/` (directory containing the pipe-delimited text data files)
         
         #### Module Responsibilities:
         
         - **app.py**
           - Initialize Flask app instance.
           - Register blueprints from `routes/`.
           - Setup session configuration and error handlers.
         
         - **routes/**
           - Define route handlers (controller functions) mapped to HTTP routes.
           - Handle request input (GET/POST data).
           - Coordinate calls to `services` and `models` modules.
           - Render templates with provided context variables.
         
         - **models/**
           - Encapsulate reading/writing to the data text files (`users.txt`, `articles.txt`, etc.).
           - Each data file has a corresponding model module class or functions to parse, update, and save records.
           - Provide methods to query/filter data for listing and retrieval by ID.
           - Handle concurrency by file locking if needed during writes.
         
         - **services/**
           - Implement business logic including article creation, editing, versioning, approval workflow.
           - Coordinate multi-model interactions (e.g., saving an article update alongside creating a version record).
           - Handle validation logic for input data.
           - Manage approval workflows and version history data aggregation for display.
         
         - **utils/**
           - Contain helpers for parsing date/time, generating IDs for new records.
           - Provide session helpers and authentication stubs.
           - File-based utilities for safe read/write of pipe-delimited data.
         
         - **data/**
           - Storage location for all app data text files.
           - These files are accessed only via `models/` to enforce encapsulation.
         
         ### Data Flow Between Components
         
         1. **Incoming HTTP request** reaches a route defined in `routes/`.
         2. Route handler extracts input from request (URL params, form data).
         3. For data retrieval or updates, route calls `services/` for business logic.
         4. `services/` interacts with one or more `models/` modules to fetch/update data files.
         5. Validation and version control logic applies in `services/`.
         6. Aggregated data is returned to the route, which then renders a template passing context.
         
         This layered design creates clear separation between routing, business logic, and data access.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 2: Routing and API Endpoints
         
         Below is the detailed list of Flask routes derived from design_spec.md with methods, functions, and input/output.
         
         | Route Pattern                     | HTTP Method(s) | Controller Function      | Input/Output Description                                    |
         |---------------------------------|----------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------|
         | `/dashboard`                    | GET            | `dashboard()`           | Input: session user
         Output: renders `dashboard.html` with `username` (str). |
         | `/article/create`               | GET, POST      | `create_article()`      | GET: No input, displays form.
         POST: Form data for new article draft.
         Output: on success redirect; on error, render with validation errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/edit`| GET, POST      | `edit_article(article_id)`| GET: loads article data and versions.
         POST: updated article data for new version.
         Output: render `edit_article.html` with `article` dict and `version_history` list or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/versions`| GET         | `version_history(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch versions.
         Output: renders `version_history.html` with versions list and optional comparison data. |
         | `/articles/mine`                | GET            | `my_articles()`         | Input: current user session.
         Output: list of user's articles and filter status. |
         | `/articles/published`           | GET            | `published_articles()`  | Input: optional query params for category filter and sort order.
         Output: list of published articles. |
         | `/calendar`                    | GET, POST      | `content_calendar()`    | GET: render with publication schedule data and view selector.
         POST: receives scheduling data.
         Output: updated schedule or errors. |
         | `/article/<int:article_id>/analytics`| GET        | `article_analytics(article_id)`| Input: `article_id` to fetch analytics.
         Output: renders analytics data structured for display. |
         
         ### Route Input & Output Details
         
         - Routes supporting POST will handle JSON/form submissions with validation. Validation errors are passed back to templates as context.
         - Dynamic routes use `<int:article_id>` capturing article identifiers directly as integers.
         - User session management (e.g. current username) is consistently obtained from Flask session.
         - Authentication is presumed to be handled externally or in middleware; session correctness assumed.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 3: Version Control Design
         
         ### Architecture for Article Versioning and Approval Workflow
         
         - **Article Versions:**
           - Stored in `article_versions.txt`, each row represents a version with fields:
             - `version_id` (unique),
             - `article_id` link,
             - `version_number` (incremented per article),
             - `content` (full textual content),
             - `author` username,
             - `created_date` timestamp,
             - `change_summary` (one-line description).
           - New versions created on edits.
         
         - **Approval Workflow:**
           - Approvals stored in `approvals.txt` linking to specific article versions.
           - Each approval entry:
             - `approval_id` unique,
             - `article_id`,
             - `version_id`,
             - `approver` username,
             - `status` (approved, rejected, revision_requested),
             - `comments` text,
             - `timestamp`.
           - Multiple approvers may act on same version.
         
         - **Comments:**
           - Comments linked to specific versions in `comments.txt`.
         
         - **Workflow Stages:**
           - Defined per category in `workflow_stages.txt`.
           - Used to guide or validate article progress through editorial process.
         
         ### Interaction with Storage
         
         - On article edit:
           - `services` creates a new version_id with incremented version_number.
           - Saves content and metadata to `article_versions.txt`.
         
         - On approval action:
           - Approval records appended to `approvals.txt`.
         
         - Fetching version history combines data from `article_versions.txt` and related approvals/comments.
         
         - Version comparison data computed in business logic layer by loading relevant versions.
         
         ---
         
         ## Section 4: Frontend Integration Points
         
         - Backend renders templates specifying exact context variables as per page requirements.
         - Context variables include:
           - Simple types (str, int) e.g., `username`, `article_id`.
           - Collections (list of dicts) e.g., lists of articles, versions, analytics data.
           - Complex dict structures representing article data, version details, and analytics.
         
         - JSON-serializable data is passed embedded in templates to enable frontend JS consumption.
         
         - Backend ensures data consistency and necessary pre-processing (like date formatting) before passing.
         
         - Coordination Points with Frontend Team:
           - Naming and structure of context variables must match frontend expectations (keys in dicts, field names).
           - Data structures for version histories must support rendering versions list and diffs.
           - Error message structures on form POSTs must be standardized for frontend display.
           - Pagination or filtering parameters should be planned between backend query handling and frontend controls.
         
         - Navigation elements delegate routing to backend URLs; frontend triggers GET or POST requests accordingly.
         
         - Templates rely on backend for initial data load; frontend may leverage embedded JSON for dynamic components.
         
         ---
         
         This architecture documentation provides the backend design foundation covering the Flask application structure, detailed routing, version control management, and frontend integration approach needed to implement and coordinate development of the ContentPublishingHub application.
         
         All implementation should adhere strictly to the version-controlled flat-file storage conventions and template data contracts defined here.

         from flask import Flask, request, jsonify, redirect, url_for, session
         import os
         import csv
         import threading
         import datetime
         import uuid
         
         app = Flask(__name__)
         app.secret_key = 'supersecretkey'
         
         lock = threading.Lock()
         
         DATA_DIR = 'data'
         ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'article_versions.txt')
         APPROVALS_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'approvals.txt')
         ARTICLES_FILE = os.path.join(DATA_DIR, 'articles.txt')  # assumed for basic article metadata storage
         
         # Util functions
         
         def read_pipe_delimited_file(filepath):
             data = []
             if not os.path.exists(filepath):
                 return data
             with open(filepath, 'r', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                 reader = csv.DictReader(f, delimiter='|')
                 for row in reader:
                     data.append(row)
             return data
         
         
         def write_pipe_delimited_file(filepath, data, fieldnames):
             with lock:
                 with open(filepath, 'w', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     writer = csv.DictWriter(f, fieldnames=fieldnames, delimiter='|')
                     writer.writeheader()
                     for row in data:
                         writer.writerow(row)
         
         
         def append_pipe_delimited_file(filepath, row, fieldnames):
             # Append a single row to file
             with lock:
                 file_exists = os.path.exists(filepath)
                 with open(filepath, 'a', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                     writer = csv.DictWriter(f, fieldnames=fieldnames, delimiter='|')
                     if not file_exists:
                         writer.writeheader()
                     writer.writerow(row)
         
         
         # Generate unique IDs
         
         def generate_uuid():
             return str(uuid.uuid4())
         
         
         def current_timestamp():
             return datetime.datetime.utcnow().isoformat() + 'Z'
         
         
         # Routes
         
         @app.route('/')
         def root():
             # Redirect root to dashboard
             return redirect(url_for('dashboard'))
         
         
         @app.route('/dashboard')
         def dashboard():
             # Return session info and summary data, stub implementation
             user = session.get('username', 'guest')
             # For simplicity, list articles and versions count
             articles = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLES_FILE)
             article_summaries = []
             for art in articles:
                 article_id = art.get('article_id')
                 versions = [v for v in read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE) if v['article_id'] == article_id]
                 article_summaries.append({
                     'article_id': article_id,
                     'title': art.get('title', ''),
                     'versions_count': len(versions)
                 })
             return jsonify({
                 'session_user': user,
                 'articles': article_summaries
             })
         
         
         @app.route('/article/create', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def create_article():
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 form = request.form
                 title = form.get('title')
                 content = form.get('content')
                 author = session.get('username', 'anonymous')
         
                 if not title or not content:
                     return jsonify({'error': 'Title and content are required'}), 400
         
                 # Create a new article entry
                 article_id = generate_uuid()
         
                 # Save basic article metadata
                 articles = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLES_FILE)
                 articles.append({'article_id': article_id, 'title': title, 'author': author})
                 write_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLES_FILE, articles, fieldnames=['article_id', 'title', 'author'])
         
                 # Create initial version
                 version_id = generate_uuid()
                 version_row = {
                     'version_id': version_id,
                     'article_id': article_id,
                     'version_number': '1',
                     'content': content,
                     'username': author,
                     'change_summary': 'Initial version',
                     'timestamp': current_timestamp()
                 }
                 append_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, version_row, fieldnames=version_row.keys())
         
                 return jsonify({'message': 'Article created', 'article_id': article_id, 'version_id': version_id})
             else:
                 # For GET, we only return a placeholder as no frontend templates
                 return jsonify({'info': 'Send POST request with title and content to create article'})
         
         
         @app.route('/article/<string:article_id>/edit', methods=['GET', 'POST'])
         def edit_article(article_id):
             articles = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLES_FILE)
             article = next((a for a in articles if a['article_id'] == article_id), None)
             if article is None:
                 return jsonify({'error': 'Article not found'}), 404
         
             if request.method == 'POST':
                 form = request.form
                 content = form.get('content')
                 change_summary = form.get('change_summary', '')
                 username = session.get('username', 'anonymous')
         
                 if not content:
                     return jsonify({'error': 'Content is required to create a new version'}), 400
         
                 # Load versions to determine next version number
                 versions = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE)
                 article_versions = [v for v in versions if v['article_id'] == article_id]
                 if article_versions:
                     max_version = max(int(v['version_number']) for v in article_versions)
                     next_version = max_version + 1
                 else:
                     next_version = 1
         
                 version_id = generate_uuid()
                 new_version = {
                     'version_id': version_id,
                     'article_id': article_id,
                     'version_number': str(next_version),
                     'content': content,
                     'username': username,
                     'change_summary': change_summary,
                     'timestamp': current_timestamp()
                 }
                 append_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE, new_version, fieldnames=new_version.keys())
         
                 return jsonify({'message': 'Article version updated', 'version_id': version_id})
             else:
                 # For GET, return article data and version history
                 versions = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE)
                 version_history = [v for v in versions if v['article_id'] == article_id]
                 version_history.sort(key=lambda x: int(x['version_number']))
                 return jsonify({
                     'article': article,
                     'version_history': version_history
                 })
         
         
         @app.route('/article/<string:article_id>/approve', methods=['POST'])
         def approve_article(article_id):
             form = request.form
             version_id = form.get('version_id')
             status = form.get('status')  # e.g. approved, rejected
             comment = form.get('comment', '')
             username = session.get('username', 'anonymous')
         
             if not version_id or not status:
                 return jsonify({'error': 'version_id and status are required'}), 400
         
             # Store approval entry
             approval_id = generate_uuid()
             approval_entry = {
                 'approval_id': approval_id,
                 'version_id': version_id,
                 'article_id': article_id,
                 'username': username,
                 'status': status,
                 'comment': comment,
                 'timestamp': current_timestamp()
             }
             append_pipe_delimited_file(APPROVALS_FILE, approval_entry, fieldnames=approval_entry.keys())
         
             return jsonify({'message': 'Approval recorded', 'approval_id': approval_id})
         
         
         @app.route('/article/<string:article_id>/comments', methods=['POST'])
         def add_comment(article_id):
             form = request.form
             version_id = form.get('version_id')
             comment_text = form.get('comment')
             username = session.get('username', 'anonymous')
         
             if not version_id or not comment_text:
                 return jsonify({'error': 'version_id and comment text are required'}), 400
         
             # Append comment to approvals with a comment type but status empty
             comment_entry = {
                 'approval_id': generate_uuid(),
                 'version_id': version_id,
                 'article_id': article_id,
                 'username': username,
                 'status': '',
                 'comment': comment_text,
                 'timestamp': current_timestamp()
             }
             append_pipe_delimited_file(APPROVALS_FILE, comment_entry, fieldnames=comment_entry.keys())
         
             return jsonify({'message': 'Comment added'})
         
         
         @app.route('/article/<string:article_id>/analytics')
         def article_analytics(article_id):
             # Stub analytics response - could provide views, unique visitors, approval stats
             # For now just count versions and approvals
             versions = read_pipe_delimited_file(ARTICLE_VERSIONS_FILE)
             version_count = len([v for v in versions if v['article_id'] == article_id])
             approvals = read_pipe_delimited_file(APPROVALS_FILE)
             approval_count = len([a for a in approvals if a['article_id'] == article_id and a['status'] == 'approved'])
         
             return jsonify({
                 'article_id': article_id,
                 'version_count': version_count,
                 'approved_count': approval_count
             })
         
         
         if __name__ == '__main__':
             # Ensure data directory exists
             os.makedirs(DATA_DIR, exist_ok=True)
             app.run(debug=True)

      File: /home/jun/0624/CaMP/results/Software-web-ablation/20260121_000000_677638_0.2_compound_only_self/ContentPublishingHub/compound_chaos/app.py
